Gandhi Day of Service event year after year. 1. What motivated you to start Gandhi Day? I used to host this event in college and we were able to integrate it with the IACC 5 years ago on a larger scale. The IACC has been successful with providing a platform to network and build business relationships. When I brought this to the board, they agreed it would be equally valuable, if not more, to stay true to our roots and host an event geared around “seva” (selfless service). 2. Besides feeding the children, why is this charitable community event rewarding for you. My parents made sure that volunteering and acts of kindness were a part of our life growing up. From a young age, it has been instilled in me. Aside from the meals we provide and the community coming together, its rewarding to see so many children attending year after year. As they grow up, hopefully they will be able to continue to pay it forward. 3. What is your goal for next year? The sky's the limit. We're very fortunate that our members and the community have helped us take this to the next level. We will continue to surpass the previous year’s number with a goal of packaging 1 million meals one day! 4. What advice do you give to your fellow Indian American friends to remain engaged in the community? The community encompasses our family and friends. The quote that pushes Gandhi Day forward, \"Be the change you want to see in the world.\" is the reason engaging in our community is so important. Every person and every task, whether small or big, can add up to make a big difference. 5. How can people become involved with Gandhi Day 2020? There are numerous ways to be involved with Gandhi Day. From simply volunteering to securing sponsorships and everything in between. As we aim to make this bigger every year, the planning will start early in the year. Anyone interested can contact myself or an IACC board member. It's a collective effort that makes this event so
